	<div><!-- duplicate React-root div for styling -->
	<div class="content">
		<article class="article-container article--post ">
			<header class="article__header article-featured__header">
	<div class="article__title-wrapper">
						<h1 class="article__title">Volvo to use Luminar&#8217;s lidar in production vehicles to unlock automated driving on highways</h1>
			<h2 class="article__subtitle">Starting in 2022 with the XC90</h2>
		</div>

			<div class="article__byline-wrapper">
			
<div class="article__byline">
			<a href="https://techcrunch.com/author/kirsten-korosec/">
			Kirsten Korosec		</a>
		<span class="article__byline__meta">
						8 hours		</span>
	</div>
		</div>
	
	</header>

			<div class="article-content">
				<p id="speakable-summary"><span class="featured__span-first-words">Volvo Cars will</span> start producing vehicles in 2020 that are equipped with lidar and a perception stack — technology developed by Silicon Valley startup Luminar that the automaker will use to deploy an automated driving system for highways.</p>
<p>For now, the lidar will be part of a hardware package that consumers can add as an option to their Volvo vehicle, starting with the second-generation XC90. Volvo will combine <a class="crunchbase-link" href="https://crunchbase.com/organization/luminar-technologies" target="_blank" data-type="organization" data-entity="luminar-technologies">Luminar&#8217;s <span class="crunchbase-tooltip-indicator"></span></a> lidar with cameras, radar, software and back-up systems for functions such as steering, braking and battery power to enable its highway pilot feature.</p>
<p>Volvo, which is known for making its advanced safety features standard, sees a bigger opportunity in its partnership with Luminar. The Swedish automaker said Luminar will help it improve advanced driver assistance systems and may lead to all of its second-generation Scalable Product Architecture (SPA2) vehicles to come with lidar as a standard feature.</p>
<p>Luminar and Volvo didn&#8217;t reveal how much this highway pilot package might cost. Luminar has previously said its Iris lidar unit will cost less than $1,000 per unit for production vehicles seeking full autonomy and about $500 for version used for more limited purposes like driver assistance.</p>
<p>The announcement is a milestone for Luminar and its whiz founder <a class="crunchbase-link" href="https://crunchbase.com/person/austin-russell" target="_blank" data-type="person" data-entity="austin-russell">Austin Russell, <span class="crunchbase-tooltip-indicator"></span></a> who burst onto the autonomous vehicle startup scene <a href="https://techcrunch.com/2017/04/13/luminar-debuts-a-sensor-to-make-self-driving-cars-safer-than-human/">in April 2017</a> after operating for years in secrecy. It also makes Volvo the first automaker to equip production vehicles with lidar — the light detection and ranging radar that measures distance using laser light to generate a highly accurate 3D map of the world around the car.</p>
<p>Luminar&#8217;s Iris lidar sensors — which <a class="crunchbase-link" href="https://crunchbase.com/organization/techcrunch" target="_blank" data-type="organization" data-entity="techcrunch">TechCrunch <span class="crunchbase-tooltip-indicator"></span></a> has described as about the size of really thick sandwich and one-third smaller than its previous iterations — will be integrated in the roof. The sensor&#8217;s tucked away placement is a departure from the bucket style spinning lidars that have become synonymous with autonomous vehicle development.</p>
<p><div id="attachment_1984654" style="width: 4106px" class="wp-caption alignnone"><a href="https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/Volvo_SPA2_Luminar_Roofline_Integration-1.png"><img aria-describedby="caption-attachment-1984654" class="breakout wp-image-1984654 size-full" src="https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/Volvo_SPA2_Luminar_Roofline_Integration-1.png" alt="" width="4096" height="2160" srcset="https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/Volvo_SPA2_Luminar_Roofline_Integration-1.png 4096w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/Volvo_SPA2_Luminar_Roofline_Integration-1.png?resize=150,79 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/Volvo_SPA2_Luminar_Roofline_Integration-1.png?resize=300,158 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/Volvo_SPA2_Luminar_Roofline_Integration-1.png?resize=768,405 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/Volvo_SPA2_Luminar_Roofline_Integration-1.png?resize=680,359 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/Volvo_SPA2_Luminar_Roofline_Integration-1.png?resize=1536,810 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/Volvo_SPA2_Luminar_Roofline_Integration-1.png?resize=2048,1080 2048w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/Volvo_SPA2_Luminar_Roofline_Integration-1.png?resize=50,26 50w" sizes="(max-width: 4096px) 100vw, 4096px" /></a><p id="caption-attachment-1984654" class="wp-caption-text"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> Volvo</p></div></p>
<p>Shipping a vehicle with the proper hardware and perception stack doesn&#8217;t mean customers will be able to let their Volvo take over driving on highways from the get go. The software, which is being developed by <a class="crunchbase-link" href="https://crunchbase.com/organization/zenuity" target="_blank" data-type="organization" data-entity="zenuity">Zenuity, <span class="crunchbase-tooltip-indicator"></span></a> is still underway, Volvo CTO Henrik Green said.</p>
<p>The software will be activated wirelessly once it is verified to be safe in individual geographic locations. Volvo will continue to expand the capability of the software such as pushing up the maximum speed a vehicle can travel while driving autonomously. This hardware first-continual software update strategy is similar to <a class="crunchbase-link" href="https://crunchbase.com/organization/tesla-motors" target="_blank" data-type="organization" data-entity="tesla-motors">Tesla, <span class="crunchbase-tooltip-indicator"></span></a> which has sold an automated driving package to consumers for years that has improved over time, but still does not allow for so-called &#8220;full self-driving.&#8221;</p>
<p>&#8220;Soon, your Volvo will be able to drive autonomously on highways when the car determines it is safe to do so,&#8221; Green said. &#8220;At that point, your Volvo takes responsibility for the driving and you can relax, take your eyes off the road and your hands off the wheel. Over time, updates over the air will expand the areas in which the car can drive itself. For us, a safe introduction of autonomy is a gradual introduction.&#8221;</p>
<h2>A turning point for lidar</h2>
<p>Lidar sensors are considered by many automakers and tech companies an essential piece of technology to safely roll out autonomous vehicles. In the past 18 months, as the timeline to deploy commercial robotaxi fleets has expanded, automakers have turned back to developing nearer term tech for production vehicles.</p>
<p>&#8220;It&#8217;s a very isolated problem to solve and becomes a lot more solvable in a safe way than trying to solve autonomous driving through the inner city of Los Angeles or San Francisco,&#8221; Green said. &#8220;By narrowing the use case to those particular highways, we can bring safe autonomy into vehicles for personal use in the timeframe we&#8217;re talking about.&#8221;</p>
<p>Advanced driver assistance systems, or ADAS, that was pushed aside in pursuit of fully autonomous vehicles has become a darling once again. It&#8217;s prompted a pivot within the industry, particularly with lidar companies. Dozens of lidar startups once grappling to become the supplier of choice for fully driverless vehicles are now hawking their wares for use in regular old passenger cars, trucks and SUVs. Some lidar startups such as Luminar have developed the perception software as well in an effort to diversify their business and offer a more appealing package to automakers.</p>
<p>The companies will deepen their collaboration to ensure Luminar&#8217;s lidar technology is validated for series production. Volvo Cars said it has signed an agreement to possibly increase its minority stake in Luminar.</p>
<p>Luminar built its lidar from scratch, a lengthy process that it says has resulted in a simpler design and better performance. The company made a leap forward in April 2018 with the introduction of a<a href="https://techcrunch.com/2018/04/12/luminar-puts-its-lidar-tech-into-production-through-acquisitions-and-smart-engineering/"> new lidar unit</a> that performs better, is cheaper and is able to be assembled in minutes rather than hours. Luminar also acquired Black Forest Engineering as part of its strategy to improve the quality along with efficiency. And it opened a 136,000-square-foot manufacturing center in Orlando, Florida, where it does all of its engineering and development as well as the mass manufacturing.</p>
<p>The startup has continued to improve its lidar as well as attract investors. Luminar announced last year it had <a href="https://www.businesswire.com/news/home/20190711005233/en/Luminar-Drives-Expansion-Automotive-Market-250-Million">raised $100 million</a>, bringing its total to more than $250 million. The company unveiled a perception platform and its compact Iris lidar unit, which will now go into the Volvo.</p>
<p>&#8220;This is really kind of the holy grail that we&#8217;ve been working towards for the entire course of the business,&#8221; Russell said.</p>
			</div>

And the firm felt it coming.<\/p>\n<p>Sequoia <a href=\"https:\/\/medium.com\/sequoia-capital\/coronavirus-the-black-swan-of-2020-7c72bdeb9753\">published a memo on March 5<\/a> warning of a drop in business activity, supply chain disruptions and a significant softening of private financings. How should business leaders go about adapting their strategies and plowing through? What metrics should those leaders focus on both internally and in the process of fundraising?<\/p>\n<p>We&#8217;re going to chat with Botha about all that and much more, including his predictions on economic recovery, the sectors he&#8217;s particularly bullish on right now, how he&#8217;s evaluating companies during this time, and what Silicon Valley may look like in a post-COVID world. capital","slug":"sequoia-capital","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/245607"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=245607"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=245607"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=245607"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=245607"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[{"id":270121999,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?taxonomy=_tc_cb_tag_taxonomy&term=sequoia-capital-organization","name":"sequoia-capital-organization","slug":"sequoia-capital-organization","taxonomy":"_tc_cb_tag_taxonomy","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/crunchbase_tag\/270121999"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/crunchbase_tag"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/_tc_cb_tag_taxonomy"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?crunchbase_tag=270121999"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[]]}},{"id":1984513,"date":"2020-05-06T04:41:02","date_gmt":"2020-05-06T11:41:02","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=1984513"},"modified":"2020-05-06T07:48:52","modified_gmt":"2020-05-06T14:48:52","slug":"no-cookie-consent-walls-and-no-scrolling-isnt-consent-says-eu-data-protection-body","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/05\/06\/no-cookie-consent-walls-and-no-scrolling-isnt-consent-says-eu-data-protection-body\/","title":{"rendered":"No cookie consent walls &#8212; and no, scrolling isn&#8217;t consent, says EU data protection body"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">You can&#8217;t make access to your website&#8217;s content dependent on a visitor agreeing that you can process their data &#8212; aka a &#8216;consent cookie wall&#8217;. Not if you need to be compliant with European data protection law.<\/p>\n<p>That&#8217;s the unambiguous message from the European Data Protection Board (EDPB), which has published <a href=\"https:\/\/edpb.europa.eu\/sites\/edpb\/files\/files\/file1\/edpb_guidelines_202005_consent_en.pdf\">updated guidelines<\/a> on the rules around online consent to process people&#8217;s data.<\/p>\n<p>Under pan-EU law, consent is one of six lawful bases that data controllers can use when processing people&#8217;s personal data.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>But in order for consent to be legally valid under Europe&#8217;s General Data Protection Regulation (GDPR) there are specific standards to meet: It must be clear and informed, specific and freely given.<\/p>\n<p>Hence cookie walls that demand &#8216;consent&#8217; as the price for getting inside the club are not only an oxymoron but run into a legal brick wall.<\/p>\n<h2>No consent behind a cookie wall<\/h2>\n<p>The regional cookie wall has been crumbling for some time, as we <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2019\/03\/08\/cookie-walls-dont-comply-with-gdpr-says-dutch-dpa\/\">reported last year<\/a> &#8212; when the Dutch DPA clarified its guidance to ban cookie walls.<\/p>\n<p>The <a href=\"https:\/\/edpb.europa.eu\/sites\/edpb\/files\/files\/file1\/edpb_guidelines_202005_consent_en.pdf\">updated guidelines<\/a> from the EDPB look intended to hammer the point home. The steering body&#8217;s role is to provide guidance to national data protection agencies to encourage a more consistent application of data protection rules.<\/p>\n<p>The EDPB&#8217;s intervention should &#8212; should! &#8212; remove any inconsistencies of interpretation on the updated points by national agencies of the bloc&#8217;s 27 Member States. (Though compliance with EU data protection law tends to be a process; aka it&#8217;s a marathon not a sprint, though on the cookie wall issues the &#8216;runners&#8217; have been going around the tracks for a considerable time now.)<\/p>\n<p>As we noted in our report on the Dutch clarification last year, the Internet Advertising Bureau Europe was operating a full cookie wall &#8212; instructing visitors to &#8216;agree&#8217; to its data processing terms if they wished to view the content.<\/p>\n<p>The problem that we pointed out is that that wasn&#8217;t a free choice. Yet EU law requires a free choice for consent to be legally valid. So it&#8217;s interesting to note the IAB Europe has, at some point since, updated its cookie consent implementation &#8212; removing the cookie wall and offering a fairly clear (if nudged) choice to visitors to either accept or deny cookies for &#8220;aggregated statistics&#8221;&#8230;<\/p>\n<p><img class=\"breakout aligncenter wp-image-1984515 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Screenshot-2020-05-06-at-12.10.18.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"2764\" height=\"208\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Screenshot-2020-05-06-at-12.10.18.png 2764w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Screenshot-2020-05-06-at-12.10.18.png?resize=150,11 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Screenshot-2020-05-06-at-12.10.18.png?resize=300,23 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Screenshot-2020-05-06-at-12.10.18.png?resize=768,58 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Screenshot-2020-05-06-at-12.10.18.png?resize=680,51 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Screenshot-2020-05-06-at-12.10.18.png?resize=1536,116 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Screenshot-2020-05-06-at-12.10.18.png?resize=2048,154 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Screenshot-2020-05-06-at-12.10.18.png?resize=50,4 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 2764px) 100vw, 2764px\" \/><\/p>\n<p>As we said at the time the writing was on the wall for consent cookie walls.<\/p>\n<p>The EDPB document includes the below example to illustrate the salient point that consent cookie walls do not &#8220;constitute valid consent, as the provision of the service relies on the data subject clicking the &#8216;Accept cookies&#8217; button. It is not presented with a genuine choice.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>It&#8217;s hard to get clearer than that, really.<\/p>\n<p><img class=\"size-large wp-image-1984518 aligncenter\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Screenshot-2020-05-06-at-12.28.43.png?w=680\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"171\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Screenshot-2020-05-06-at-12.28.43.png 1390w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Screenshot-2020-05-06-at-12.28.43.png?resize=150,38 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Screenshot-2020-05-06-at-12.28.43.png?resize=300,76 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Screenshot-2020-05-06-at-12.28.43.png?resize=768,193 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Screenshot-2020-05-06-at-12.28.43.png?resize=680,171 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Screenshot-2020-05-06-at-12.28.43.png?resize=50,13 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" \/><\/p>\n<h2>Scrolling never means &#8216;take my data&#8217;<\/h2>\n<p>A second area to get attention in the updated guidance, as a result of the EDPB deciding there was a need for additional clarification, is the issue of scrolling and consent.<\/p>\n<p>Simply put: Scrolling on a website or digital service can not &#8212; in any way &#8212; be interpreted as consent.<\/p>\n<p>Or, as the EDPB puts it, &#8220;actions such as scrolling or swiping through a webpage or similar user activity will not <strong>under any circumstances<\/strong> satisfy the requirement of a clear and affirmative action&#8221; [emphasis ours].<\/p>\n<p>Logical reason being such signals are not unambiguous. (Additionally, the EDPB example raises the point of how would a user withdraw consent if such a signal were valid? By scrolling back up the same web page? Obviously that would be ridiculous and confusing.)<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"550\" data-dnt=\"true\">\n<p lang=\"en\" dir=\"ltr\">The gem in the updated guidelines on <a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/hashtag\/GDPR?src=hash&amp;ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">#GDPR<\/a> consent saying when action on a website may or may not constitute valid consent. Random user activity is not consent, for many reasons. Best reason: how to withdraw consent with equally random user activity? ;-) <a href=\"https:\/\/t.co\/lRmtFySA8Q\">https:\/\/t.co\/lRmtFySA8Q<\/a> <a href=\"https:\/\/t.co\/XktzldSUH0\">pic.twitter.com\/XktzldSUH0<\/a><\/p>\n<p>&mdash; Lukasz Olejnik (@lukOlejnik) <a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/lukOlejnik\/status\/1257961751360016385?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">May 6, 2020<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><script async src=\"https:\/\/platform.twitter.com\/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"><\/script><\/div>\n<p>Here&#8217;s the relevant example from the document:<\/p>\n<p><img class=\"size-large wp-image-1984521 aligncenter\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Screenshot-2020-05-06-at-12.46.37.png?w=680\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"139\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Screenshot-2020-05-06-at-12.46.37.png 1372w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Screenshot-2020-05-06-at-12.46.37.png?resize=150,31 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Screenshot-2020-05-06-at-12.46.37.png?resize=300,61 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Screenshot-2020-05-06-at-12.46.37.png?resize=768,157 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Screenshot-2020-05-06-at-12.46.37.png?resize=680,139 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Screenshot-2020-05-06-at-12.46.37.png?resize=50,10 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" \/><\/p>\n<p>Again, harder to get clearer than that.<\/p>\n<p>So any websites still trying to drop tracking cookies the moment a site visitor scrolls the page are risking regulatory enforcement. (Reminder: GDPR fines can scale as high as \u20ac20M or 4% of global annual turnover.)<\/p>\n<p>Nonetheless, <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2019\/08\/10\/most-eu-cookie-consent-notices-are-meaningless-or-manipulative-study-finds\/\">recent research<\/a> suggests cookie consent theatre remains rife in the EU &#8212; albeit, not only limited to the &#8216;scroll and you&#8217;ve been tracked&#8217; flavor of the practice.<\/p>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/01\/10\/cookie-consent-tools-are-being-used-to-undermine-eu-privacy-rules-study-suggests\/\">Manipulative consent pop-ups and dark patterns<\/a> also remain a major problem, with such tactics being actively deployed to undermine legal protections for EU citizens&#8217; data.<\/p>\n<p>Still, a lot of clarifying light has now been shone into this area by both regulators and courts, shrinking the operating space for bad faith actors.<\/p>\n<p>A ruling by the <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https:\/\/crunchbase.com\/organization\/european-court-of-justice\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"european-court-of-justice\">European Court of Justice <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"><\/span><\/a> <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2019\/10\/01\/europes-top-court-says-active-consent-is-needed-for-tracking-cookies\/\">last year<\/a> made it clear that active consent is required for tracking cookies, for example &#8212; also demolished &#8216;pre-checking&#8217; as a valid way of gathering consent, among other stipulations.<\/p>\n<p>Plus there&#8217;s <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/04\/27\/brave-accuses-european-governments-of-gdpr-resourcing-failure\/\">increasing pressure on regulators to actually <\/a><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/02\/19\/lack-of-big-tech-gdpr-decisions-looms-large-in-eu-watchdogs-annual-report\/\">enforce the rules<\/a> &#8212; with GDPR&#8217;s two year anniversary fast approaching.<\/p>\n<p>So where consent is concerned, the rule of thumb, if you need one, is you can&#8217;t steal consent nor conceal consent. And if you wish to shortcut consent you can only do so if your shortcut is A) clearly and accurately signposted and B) you offer a similarly easy route to opt-out again. Simples.<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>You can&#8217;t make access to your website&#8217;s content dependent on a visitor agreeing that you can process their data &#8212; aka a &#8216;consent cookie wall&#8217;. Not if you need to be compliant with European data protection law. That&#8217;s the unambiguous message from the European Data Protection Board (EDPB), which has published updated guidelines on the Board","slug":"european-data-protection-board","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576759598"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576759598"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576759598"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576759598"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576759598"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":46740,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/european-union\/","name":"european union","slug":"european-union","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/46740"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=46740"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=46740"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=46740"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=46740"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[]]}},{"id":1984560,"date":"2020-05-06T05:34:30","date_gmt":"2020-05-06T12:34:30","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=1984560"},"modified":"2020-05-06T06:22:13","modified_gmt":"2020-05-06T13:22:13","slug":"burst-oral-care-series-c","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/05\/06\/burst-oral-care-series-c\/","title":{"rendered":"Goldman Sachs backs electric toothbrush startup Burst Oral Care"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><a href=\"https:\/\/www.burstoralcare.com\/\">Burst Oral Care<\/a>, a startup that sells an electric toothbrush boasting charcoal bristles and 33,000 sonic vibrations per minute, has raised a Series C of undisclosed size.<\/p>\n<p>Although we don&#8217;t know the amount of the round, the Series C was led by Goldman Sachs Growth Equity, and Burst says it more than doubled the valuation from its previous round. (Goldman Sachs&#8217; other direct-to-consumer investments include women&#8217;s razor startup Billie, which was <a href=\"https:\/\/www.forbes.com\/sites\/andriacheng\/2020\/01\/09\/the-stakes-are-high-behind-pgs-plan-to-buy-growing-womens-shaving-brand-billie\/\">recently acquired by P&amp;G<\/a>.)<\/p>\n<p>The startup also says it has hundreds of thousands of subscribers who don&#8217;t just buy the $69.99 toothbrush but are also signed up to receive $6 replacement heads every 90 days. Co-founder and President Brittany Stewart argued that the need for a product like this has only grown in recent months, as the COVID-19 pandemic has shut down many dentists&#8217; offices (dentists were facing some of <a href=\"https:\/\/www.dentistrytoday.com\/news\/industrynews\/item\/6158-dental-professionals-face-higher-risks-of-covid-19-exposure\">the highest risks of exposure<\/a>).<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>&#8220;The only care that you&#8217;re getting is oral care at home,&#8221; Stewart said.<\/p>\n<p>As a result, she suggested that more dentists are pointing their patients to Burst as a way to keep their mouths in good shape until it&#8217;s safe to get a professional cleaning. (Meanwhile, some of the factories that Burst works with in China were closed by the pandemic, but Stewart said the company had done enough inventory planning that subscriptions were not affected.)<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_1984597\" style=\"width: 690px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-1984597\" class=\"size-large wp-image-1984597\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Founders.jpg?w=680\" alt=\"Burst founders Hamish Khayat and Brittany Stewart\" width=\"680\" height=\"579\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Founders.jpg 1374w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Founders.jpg?resize=150,128 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Founders.jpg?resize=300,255 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Founders.jpg?resize=768,654 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Founders.jpg?resize=680,579 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Founders.jpg?resize=50,43 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-1984597\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Burst founders Hamish Khayat and Brittany Stewart<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>In fact, although Burst sells its toothbrush through a direct-to-consumer, subscription e-commerce model, it reaches new customers through a network of 25,000 &#8220;ambassadors&#8221; \u2014 namely, dental professionals who get a personalized discount code and referral fee for recommending the product.<\/p>\n<p>This approach has prompted at some <a href=\"https:\/\/www.wired.com\/story\/mouth-tech\/\">skeptical comparisons to multi-level marketing programs<\/a>, but Burst and its investors have said it&#8217;s closer to an affiliate model. And during our interview, co-founder and CEO Hamish Khayat suggested that one of the startup&#8217;s real strengths compared other toothbrush and dental care startups is its involvement with the professional community.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Since we started the company, we&#8217;ve been to every single dental show, we&#8217;ve been to dental offices, and through that we&#8217;ve garnered a very different set of knowledge,&#8221; Khayat said.<\/p>\n<p>Stewart added that as Burst develops new products, it&#8217;s doing so in consultation with &#8220;thousands of dental professionals.&#8221; It&#8217;s already expanded beyond the toothbrush with products like floss, whitening strips and toothpaste, and Khayat said one of the big priorities in the comings months is launching a lineup of products for kids.<\/p>\n<p>Burst previously raised a total of $20 million in funding. As part of the new investment, Goldman&#8217;s Allison Berardo and Hillel Moerman are joining the company&#8217;s board of directors.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;We are excited to back Brittany, Hamish, and the rest of the BURST team as they harness the power of the dental community to build a next-generation oral care business,&#8221; Berardo said in a statement. &#8220;BURST has a clear vision and brand ethos and we believe they have meaningful runway ahead with regard to both their product suite and go-to-market strategy.\u201d<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"9AWI3DzHW1\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2019\/04\/09\/investors-continue-to-pour-money-into-dental-startups\/\">Investors continue to pour money into dental startups<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe title=\"&#8220;Investors continue to pour money into dental startups&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2019\/04\/09\/investors-continue-to-pour-money-into-dental-startups\/embed\/#?secret=9AWI3DzHW1\" data-secret=\"9AWI3DzHW1\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Burst Oral Care, a startup that sells an electric toothbrush boasting charcoal bristles and 33,000 sonic vibrations per minute, has raised a Series C of undisclosed size. is laying off 3,700 as rides plummet due to COVID-19"},"content":{"rendered":"<p class=\"p1\"><span class=\"s1\">In <a href=\"https:\/\/www.sec.gov\/ix?doc=\/Archives\/edgar\/data\/1543151\/000155278120000325\/e20313_uber-8k.htm\">an SEC filing<\/a> dating back to last week, Uber disclosed plans to layoff 3,700 employees. The figure amounts to around 14% percent of the ride hailing giant\u2019s total workforce. <\/span><\/p>\n<p class=\"p1\"><span class=\"s1\">In the document, the company states that the job loss is part of a planned reduction in operating expenses \u201cin response to the economic challenges and uncertainty resulting from the COVID-19 pandemic and its impact on the company\u2019s business.\u201d<\/span><\/p>\n<p class=\"p1\"><span class=\"s1\">While Uber hasn\u2019t suspended operations altogether, the company has no doubt taken a massive hit to its bottom line as state governments have issued stay at home orders for non-essential workers. <\/span><\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p class=\"p1\"><span class=\"s1\">In <a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/kateconger\/status\/1258026056235155456\">a letter to staff<\/a>, CEO Dara Khosrowshahi noted that the cuts will come from from community operations and recruiting. Uber will also be closing around 40 percent of its Greenlight locations \u2014 used for in-person driver assistance. <\/span><\/p>\n<p class=\"p1\"><span class=\"s1\">\u201cWith the reality of our rides trips volumes being down significantly, our need for CommOps as well as in-person support is down substantially,\u201d he writes. \u201cAnd with our hiring freeze, there simply isn\u2019t enough work for recruiters.&#8221;<\/span><\/p>\n<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><span class=\"s1\">Khosrowshahi has also agreed to waive his own base salary for the rest of 2020.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n<p>&#8220;In connection with the foregoing, Dara Khosrowshahi, the Company\u2019s Chief Executive Officer, after consultation with the Board of Directors, agreed to waive his base salary for the remainder of the year ending December 31, 2020,&#8221; the company writes in the filing. &#8220;In connection with this decision, Mr. Khosrowshahi and the Company entered into a letter agreement, effective as of May 2, 2020.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>The executive made around $1 million in 2019.<\/p>\n<p>We&#8217;ve reached out to <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https:\/\/crunchbase.com\/organization\/uber\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"uber\">Uber <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"><\/span><\/a> for further comment.<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>In an SEC filing dating back to last week, Uber disclosed plans to layoff 3,700 employees. The figure amounts to around 14% percent of the ride hailing giant\u2019s total workforce. /techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=217609"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=217609"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=217609"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=217609"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[]]}},{"id":1983929,"date":"2020-05-05T16:01:12","date_gmt":"2020-05-05T23:01:12","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=1983929"},"modified":"2020-05-05T15:16:26","modified_gmt":"2020-05-05T22:16:26","slug":"social-network-for-women-peanut-raises-12m-series-a-amid-pandemic","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/05\/05\/social-network-for-women-peanut-raises-12m-series-a-amid-pandemic\/","title":{"rendered":"Social network for women Peanut raises $12M Series A amid pandemic"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Peanut, an app that began as a tool for finding new mom friends, has evolved into a social network now used by 1.6 million women to discuss a range of topics, from pregnancy and parenthood to marriage and menopause, and everything in between. On the heels of significant growth in online networking fueled by the COVID-19 pandemic, the company is today announcing the close of a $12 million Series A round of funding, led by <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https:\/\/crunchbase.com\/organization\/eqtventures\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"eqtventures\">EQT Ventures, <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"><\/span><\/a> a multi-stage VC firm that invests in companies across Europe and the U.S.<\/p>\n<p>Index Ventures and Female Founders Fund also participated, bringing Peanut&#8217;s total raise to date to $21.8 million.<\/p>\n<p>The round itself closed just weeks ago &#8212; arriving at a time when the coronavirus pandemic is impacting the startup world, often <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/03\/25\/public-optimism-doesnt-convert-to-checks-founders-report\/\">drying up<\/a> venture capital for emerging companies. Some startups, as a result, have <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/layoffs\/\">laid off employees<\/a> to self-sustain, while others have sought exits or even folded.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>Peanut, on the other hand, has seen rapid growth for its platform as women looked for a supportive online environment to discuss their own concerns over how COVID-19 was impacting their lives.<\/p>\n<p>Many women participating in <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2019\/11\/13\/social-network-for-motherhood-peanut-raises-5m-expands-to-include-women-trying-to-conceive\/\">Peanut&#8217;s newer &#8220;Trying to Conceive&#8221; group,<\/a> for example, worried about their canceled IVF rounds and how to plan for the future. Current moms-to-be wanted to hear from others about how COVID-19 would impact their hospital delivery plans. And others stuck working at home with kids looked for advice and coping strategies.<\/p>\n<p><img class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-1984173\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Profiles.png?w=680\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"466\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Profiles.png 2840w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Profiles.png?resize=150,103 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Profiles.png?resize=300,206 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Profiles.png?resize=768,527 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Profiles.png?resize=680,466 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Profiles.png?resize=1536,1054 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Profiles.png?resize=2048,1405 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Profiles.png?resize=50,34 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" \/><\/p>\n<p>Since the outbreak, Peanut has seen engagement across its app increase by 30% and content consumption increase by 40%. Its total community also grew from 1 million users in December 2019 to now 1.6 million, as of April.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;We&#8217;re really lucky in that we&#8217;re growing and that we are, for the most part, untouched by what&#8217;s happening,&#8221; says Peanut founder and CEO Michelle Kennedy. &#8220;And actually, if anyone needed community more, it&#8217;s now,&#8221; she added.<\/p>\n<p>Though the pandemic has sent the app&#8217;s usage skyrocketing, it has also readjusted Peanut&#8217;s priorities with regard to its roadmap.<\/p>\n<p>Most notably, its friend-finding feature needs a rethink.<\/p>\n<p><img class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-1984194\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Discovery_Motherhood_TTC.jpg?w=680\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"680\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Discovery_Motherhood_TTC.jpg 1946w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Discovery_Motherhood_TTC.jpg?resize=150,150 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Discovery_Motherhood_TTC.jpg?resize=300,300 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Discovery_Motherhood_TTC.jpg?resize=768,769 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Discovery_Motherhood_TTC.jpg?resize=680,680 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Discovery_Motherhood_TTC.jpg?resize=1534,1536 1534w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Discovery_Motherhood_TTC.jpg?resize=32,32 32w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Discovery_Motherhood_TTC.jpg?resize=50,50 50w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Discovery_Motherhood_TTC.jpg?resize=64,64 64w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Discovery_Motherhood_TTC.jpg?resize=96,96 96w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Discovery_Motherhood_TTC.jpg?resize=128,128 128w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" \/><\/p>\n<p>Peanut originally worked as a sort of &#8220;Tinder for mom friends&#8221; &#8212; an idea that arose from Kennedy&#8217;s personal experience with how difficult it was to forge female friendships after motherhood. As the former deputy CEO at dating app Badoo and an inaugural board member at Bumble, she brought her extensive experience in matchmaking apps to Peanut, which uses a similar swipe-based mechanism.<\/p>\n<p>But COVID-19 has up-ended this side of Peanut&#8217;s business. Today, Peanut users are meeting in Zoom chat rooms to hangout or play games, but not in person.<\/p>\n<p>Kennedy says the company will try to meet these users where they are with the development of more video networking features, potentially with technology built in-house. Other plans for the new capital include improvements to the social discovery aspects of its app, the development of a web version of Peanut, and the creation of more groups beyond those focused on fertility and motherhood, which have so far been core to the Peanut experience.<\/p>\n<p><img class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-1984193\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Groups.jpg?w=680\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"680\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Groups.jpg 1946w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Groups.jpg?resize=150,150 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Groups.jpg?resize=300,300 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Groups.jpg?resize=768,769 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Groups.jpg?resize=680,680 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Groups.jpg?resize=1534,1536 1534w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Groups.jpg?resize=32,32 32w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Groups.jpg?resize=50,50 50w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Groups.jpg?resize=64,64 64w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Groups.jpg?resize=96,96 96w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Groups.jpg?resize=128,128 128w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" \/><\/p>\n<p>Specifically, the company soon plans to launch a new community focused on women living with menopause, an experience that will reach more than a billion women by 2025. Despite the fact that all women with ovaries will go through menopause, there are relatively few online communities dedicated to it &#8212; which Peanut sees as an untapped market.<\/p>\n<p>Peanut&#8217;s real strength, however, is not in the types of communities it grows on its platform, but how they&#8217;re created.<\/p>\n<p>There has not yet been a social network that focused on &#8220;building a platform for women, thinking about women&#8217;s needs and built by a women,&#8221; explains Kennedy. &#8220;So what we end up doing is using things that already exist &#8212; trying to twist them and mold them into what we need, and never getting it exactly right,&#8221; she says. &#8220;We can do better than that.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>One small example of this is the recent launch of Peanut&#8217;s &#8220;Mute Keywords&#8221; feature that allows women to remove certain types of discussions from their feeds and notifications. Some women used this to create a coronavirus-free news feed that focused on other aspects of motherhood. Others who were trying to conceive muted conversations around &#8220;pregnancy,&#8221; which they found emotionally triggering.<\/p>\n<p><img class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-1984174\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Feed.jpg?w=680\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"680\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Feed.jpg 1946w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Feed.jpg?resize=150,150 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Feed.jpg?resize=300,300 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Feed.jpg?resize=768,769 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Feed.jpg?resize=680,680 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Feed.jpg?resize=1534,1536 1534w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Feed.jpg?resize=32,32 32w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Feed.jpg?resize=50,50 50w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Feed.jpg?resize=64,64 64w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Feed.jpg?resize=96,96 96w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Feed.jpg?resize=128,128 128w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" \/><\/p>\n<p>With the Series A&#8217;s close, Peanut says Naza Metghalchi from EQT Ventures joins the company&#8217;s\u00a0majority-female board, alongside Hannah Seal from existing investor Index Ventures.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Peanut\u2019s user engagement metrics are a testament to the app&#8217;s ability to act as a true emotional companion throughout women&#8217;s journeys,&#8221; said Naza Metghalchi, venture lead and investment advisor at EQT Ventures, in a statement. &#8220;The EQT Ventures team is excited to partner with Michelle and continue to grow Peanut into a platform that serves all women at different life milestones, exploring topics beyond fertility and motherhood which have already seen such huge traction.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>The additional funding allows London-based Peanut to expand its business and hire more engineers to join its current team of just 16.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;I think having closed a round in this climate is great for the team,&#8221; says Kennedy. &#8220;It&#8217;s also great for the community because it means that we can grow the team, build quicker, build faster and develop the product more quickly,&#8221; she adds.<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Peanut, an app that began as a tool for finding new mom friends, has evolved into a social network now used by 1.6 million women to discuss a range of topics, from pregnancy and parenthood to marriage and menopause, and everything in between. great unicorn retreat"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><span class=\"featured__span-first-words\">Hello and welcome<\/span> back to our regular morning look at private companies, public markets and the gray space in between.<\/p>\n<p>Today we&#8217;re taking stock of what&#8217;s happening to a number of unicorns, both public and private. This is the third time we&#8217;ve sat down to document what feels like a wave of unicorn cuts, capped in this case by <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https:\/\/crunchbase.com\/organization\/airbnb\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"airbnb\">Airbnb&#8217;s <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"><\/span><\/a> decision to cut around a quarter of its global staff (25.3%, according to provided numbers).<\/p>\n<p>Airbnb&#8217;s cuts follow <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/04\/29\/lyft-is-laying-off-982-employees-furloughing-a-further-288-due-to-covid-19-pandemic\/\">recent excisions at Lime<\/a>, <a href=\"https:\/\/economictimes.indiatimes.com\/small-biz\/startups\/newsbuzz\/oyo-gives-pink-slips-to-us-staff\/articleshow\/75038719.cms\">Oyo<\/a>, and others. Notably the cuts are not <em>only<\/em> landing amongst the best-known unicorns. Indeed, Crunchbase News (n.b. I was once its Editor in Chief) <a href=\"https:\/\/news.crunchbase.com\/news\/unicorn-companies-account-for-high-count-of-layoffs\/\">wrote a few weeks back<\/a> that 36 unicorns had cut a known 8,416 jobs, according to <a href=\"http:\/\/layoffs.fyi\/tracker\/\">a layoff tracker<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>The numbers are now sharply higher if we only added in Airbnb&#8217;s cuts. However, looking at the same database this morning, cuts amongst late-stage startups since the prior count was assembled include reductions <a href=\"https:\/\/www.businesstoday.in\/current\/corporate\/coronavirus-impact-swiggy-layoff-1000-employees-demand-slumps\/story\/401665.html\">at Swiggy<\/a>, <a href=\"https:\/\/www.pymnts.com\/gig-economy\/2020\/deliveroo-to-lay-off-15-pct-of-staff\/\">Deliveroo<\/a>, <a href=\"https:\/\/www.calcalistech.com\/ctech\/articles\/0,7340,L-3810192,00.html\">Sisense<\/a>, <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/04\/22\/magic-leap-announces-layoffs-amid-covid-19-slowdown\/\">Magic Leap<\/a>, <a href=\"https:\/\/www.americaninno.com\/boston\/inno-news-boston\/desktop-metal-lays-off-staff-amid-coronavirus-disruption\/\">DesktopMetal<\/a>, <a href=\"https:\/\/www.channele2e.com\/business\/talent\/cohesity-layoffs-2020-cloud-data-protection\/\">Cohesity<\/a>, and others.<\/p>\n<p>TechCrunch <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/01\/23\/layoffs-reach-23andme-after-hitting-mozilla-and-the-vision-fund-portfolio\/\">first covered a wave of unicorn layoffs<\/a> towards the start of the year, when companies backed by SoftBank&#8217;s Vision Fund were rapidly trying to curtail their costs and move closer to profitability. Suddenly their chief-backer, formerly the most aggressive pool of private capital in the world was on retreat, and it was time to batten the hatches.<\/p>\n<p>Those cuts, however, felt less driven by a unicorn-wide issue and more led by quarters of overly indulgent self-aggrandizement by a number of business that ran further in the red than made sense.<\/p>\n<p>The <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/03\/30\/the-second-wave-of-unicorn-layoffs-is-brutal\/\">second wave of unicorn layoffs<\/a> came in the early days of the COVID-19 pandemic. Well-known companies like Bird, ZipRecruiter, GetAround, Sonder, TripActions, and others cut staff as the economy rapidly changed as cities and states asked regular folks to stay home.<\/p>\n<p>That post, out towards the end of March, almost looks like we published it too early in retrospect. It came before <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/04\/07\/restaurant-management-platform-toast-cuts-50-of-staff\/\">Toast dramatically cut staff<\/a> or <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/04\/06\/bouncex-cuts-staff-reduces-salaries-in-wake-of-covid-19-economic-disruptions\/\">BounceX&#8217;s own layoffs<\/a>. In other words, the trend we were discussing was just getting started.<\/p>\n<p>So let&#8217;s talk about what&#8217;s happened since our March 30 check-in on the state of unicorn employment, and why we&#8217;re now in what could be the third wave of unicorn cuts this year.<\/p>\n<p><div class=\"extra-crunch-offer-container\"><\/div>","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Today we&#8217;re VCs discuss how COVID-19 is changing the media startup landscape"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><span class=\"featured__span-first-words\">The world has<\/span> changed dramatically since May 2019 when we last surveyed venture capitalists about <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2019\/05\/06\/where-top-vcs-are-investing-in-media-entertainment-gaming\/\">the trends they were seeing in media, entertainment and gaming<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>Since then, COVID-19 and the resulting physical distancing measures have created plenty of demand for companies helping to inform and entertain us as we&#8217;re stuck at home. At the same time, there&#8217;s a dramatic reduction in ad spending, making it harder to monetize that consumer attention.<\/p>\n<p>So we checked in a variety of top VCs about the new landscape, where they&#8217;re investing and what kind of advice they&#8217;re giving their portfolio companies.<\/p>\n<p>Not all of them invest directly in what (paraphrasing Betaworks&#8217; Matt Hartman) we might call <em>media<\/em> media \u2014 the companies whose business models revolve around content creation and advertising \u2014 but each of these investors are backing startups looking to change the way we stay connected and entertained.<\/p>\n<p>Here&#8217;s who we surveyed:<\/p>\n<ul>\n<li>Kevin Zhang (Partner, Upfront Ventures)<\/li>\n<li>P\u00e4r-J\u00f6rgen (PJ) P\u00e4rson (General Partner, Northzone)<\/li>\n<li>Vasu Kulkarni (Partner, Courtside Ventures)<\/li>\n<li>MG Siegler (General Partner, GV)<\/li>\n<li>Jana Messerschmidt (Partner, Lightspeed Venture Partners)<\/li>\n<li>Matthew Hartman (Partner, Betaworks Ventures)<\/li>\n<li>Gigi Levy-Weiss (Managing Partner, NFX)<\/li>\n<\/ul>\n<p>The consensus? You can&#8217;t count on the ad business to recover in the next few months, but there are still opportunities for startups exploring new formats and new business models. And there&#8217;s still plenty of excitement about gaming and esports.<\/p>\n<p>You can read their full responses, lightly edited, below.<\/p>\n<h2>Kevin Zhang, Upfront Ventures<\/h2>\n<p><strong>What (if any) media trends are still exciting you from an investing perspective?<\/strong><\/p>\n<p>Live and interactive formats, especially shorter form, continue to be very exciting, made even more evident in this time of shelter-in-place. What has worked in China and broader Asia has not yet translated into explosive success in the West. As interesting as celebrity live broadcasts are from their homes, the lack of real interaction and participation features hampers long-term engagement and doesn&#8217;t make up for the lack of production quality.<\/p>\n<p>Modern content production technology is needed to push both production and live ops cost down while enabling more interactive and engaging formats. Game engines are one example, there&#8217;s of course <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/04\/24\/fortnite-hosted-a-psychedelic-travis-scott-concert-and-12-3m-people-watched\/\">the Travis Scott concert that just happened in Fortnite<\/a> built on the Unreal engine, but that 15-minute, pre-rendered show took months to create, we&#8217;re only just scratching the surface of what&#8217;s possible.<\/p>\n<p>One of our investments in this space is Tellie for live-action formats, another is The Wave for rendered, live formats, and we continue to look for great combinations of tech and media talent innovating on new formats.<\/p>\n<p>Speaking of gaming, multiplayer games continue to grow and grow exponentially, there is a lot to unpack in popular titles from new favorite Animal Crossing to classics like World of Warcraft to indie hits like For the King. They all have social cooperation as a core part of the game loop and design. I&#8217;d love to see more teams working on cooperative play and just overall a broader diversity in multiplayer experiences beyond purely competitive ones.<div class=\"extra-crunch-offer-container\"><\/div>","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>The world has changed dramatically since May 2019 when we last surveyed venture capitalists about the trends they were seeing in media, entertainment and gaming. Since then, COVID-19 and the resulting physical distancing measures have created plenty of demand for companies helping to inform and entertain us as we&#8217;re stuck at home. turbulent stock market is a boon to investing-focused fintech startups"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><span class=\"featured__span-first-words\">Hello and welcome<\/span> back to our regular morning look at private companies, public markets and the gray space in between.<\/p>\n<p>A few weeks back we dug into <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/04\/08\/fintechs-uneven-new-reality-has-helped-some-startups-harmed-others\/\">the boom that savings and investing apps and services were enjoying<\/a>. Companies like <a href=\"https:\/\/www.acorns.com\/\">Acorns<\/a>, <a href=\"https:\/\/www.m1finance.com\/\">M1 Finance<\/a>, <a href=\"https:\/\/robinhood.com\/us\/en\/\">Robinhood<\/a> and others were seeing rapid growth in their assets under management (AUM) and downloads. New data out today underscores how well finance apps are faring in the new, chaotic COVID-19 era.<\/p>\n<p>You can run a simple test on yourself in this case. Since, say, January of this year, have you paid more or less attention to your banking and investing related apps and, more broadly, your financial life? Perhaps you are trying to put a bit more away? Or make sure your 401k isn&#8217;t invested in something silly?<\/p>\n<p>If so, you are far from alone. To detail just how much more activity this slice of the startup world is enjoying, this morning we&#8217;re taking another look at the growth that this slice of the fintech world is undergoing. We&#8217;ll lean on some new data from a mobile app analytics provider (<a href=\"https:\/\/www.appannie.com\/en\/\">AppAnnie<\/a>) and a report from a brokerage-infra startup (<a href=\"https:\/\/drivewealth.com\/\">DriveWealth<\/a>) to get a clearer picture of where investing and savings apps are growing and just how well they are performing.<\/p>\n<h2>Investing in a network of more than 40 corporate and geographically targeted startup bootcamps, has had to bring its marquee demo day events online.<\/p>\n<p>Over the last two weeks of April, industry-focused accelerators working with startups building businesses around mobility technologies (broadly) and the future of the home joined programs in Abu Dhabi, Bangalore, <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https:\/\/crunchbase.com\/organization\/berlin\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"berlin\">Berlin, <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"><\/span><\/a> Boston, Boulder and Chicago to present their cohorts.<\/p>\n<p>Each group had roughly 10 companies pitching businesses that ran the gamut from early-childhood education to capturing precious metals from the waste streams of mining operations. There were language companies, security companies, marketing companies and even a maker of a modular sous vide product for home chefs.<\/p>\n<p>The ideas were as creative as they were varied, and while all seemed promising, about two concepts from each batch stood out above the rest.<\/p>\n<p>What follows is our completely unscientific picks of the top companies that pitched at each of these virtual <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https:\/\/crunchbase.com\/organization\/techstars\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"techstars\">Techstars <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"><\/span><\/a> demo days. the new VC show-and-tell means for signaling risk"},"content":{"rendered":"<p class=\"p1\"><span class=\"featured__span-first-words\">A month ago<\/span>, we asked several venture capitalists if they planned to change the way <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/04\/02\/how-top-vcs-investing-pace-focus-and-outlook-are-changing\/\"><span class=\"s1\">they invest or lead rounds during COVID-19<\/span><\/a> \u2014 most said no, but they noted that valuations were coming down and founders in their portfolio companies were responding to the crisis.<\/p>\n<p class=\"p1\"><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/04\/02\/how-top-vcs-investing-pace-focus-and-outlook-are-changing\/\">Northzone\u2019s Paul Murphy<\/a> predicted fewer FOMO rounds because investors will \u201ctake more time to get to know and diligence the business&#8230; and it might also take a bit more time to close deals,&#8221; adding that he would &#8220;continue to lead rounds and back great founders.\u201d\u00a0But, as other <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/04\/09\/its-bullshit-that-vcs-are-open-for-business-right-now-but-that-could-change-in-a-month\/\"><span class=\"s1\">investors call their bluffs<\/span><\/a>, firms are looking for tangible ways to show they are open for business.<\/p>\n<h2 class=\"p1\"><b>First Round Capital\u00a0<\/b><\/h2>\n<p class=\"p1\">At least that was the case with <a href=\"https:\/\/firstround.com\/\">First Round Capital<\/a>. On Thursday, the seed-stage firm announced that when it leads a first round in a company, it will always take pro rata in the next outside-led venture round with a commitment of up to $3 million.<\/p>\n<p class=\"p1\">Pro rata is a clause in an investment agreement that gives the investor a right to participate in future financings. If investors don\u2019t invest in a company\u2019s pro rata, that might negatively signal they don\u2019t believe in the company\u2019s future. I asked <a href=\"https:\/\/firstround.com\/person\/brett-berson\/\">Brett Berson<\/a>, a partner at First Round, to offer more context about the announcement.<\/p>\n<p class=\"p1\">\u201cThe question &#8216;is your investor taking their pro rata&#8217; is not necessarily a checkbox answer,\u201d Berson said. \u201cAnd I think in a time of maximum uncertainty, what a given investor was doing 12 months ago might not be what he or she is doing today.\u201d<div class=\"extra-crunch-offer-container\"><\/div>","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>A month ago, we asked several venture capitalists if they planned to change the way they invest or lead rounds during COVID-19 \u2014 most said no, but they noted that valuations were coming down and founders in their portfolio companies were responding to the crisis. Link","children":[]}]},"playlistData":{"homepage":[],"videohub":[]},"entities":{"posts":[{"id":1984465,"date":"2020-05-06T07:23:39","date_gmt":"2020-05-06T14:23:39","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=1984465"},"modified":"2020-05-06T07:55:04","modified_gmt":"2020-05-06T14:55:04","slug":"volvo-to-use-luminars-lidar-in-production-vehicles-to-unlock-automated-driving-on-highways","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/05\/06\/volvo-to-use-luminars-lidar-in-production-vehicles-to-unlock-automated-driving-on-highways\/","title":{"rendered":"Volvo to use Luminar&#8217;s lidar in production vehicles to unlock automated driving on highways"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><span class=\"featured__span-first-words\">Volvo Cars will<\/span> start producing vehicles in 2020 that are equipped with lidar and a perception stack \u2014 technology developed by Silicon Valley startup Luminar that the automaker will use to deploy an automated driving system for highways.<\/p>\n<p>For now, the lidar will be part of a hardware package that consumers can add as an option to their Volvo vehicle, starting with the second-generation XC90. Volvo will combine <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https:\/\/crunchbase.com\/organization\/luminar-technologies\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"luminar-technologies\">Luminar&#8217;s <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"><\/span><\/a> lidar with cameras, radar, software and back-up systems for functions such as steering, braking and battery power to enable its highway pilot feature.<\/p>\n<p>Volvo, which is known for making its advanced safety features standard, sees a bigger opportunity in its partnership with Luminar. The Swedish automaker said Luminar will help it improve advanced driver assistance systems and may lead to all of its second-generation Scalable Product Architecture (SPA2) vehicles to come with lidar as a standard feature.<\/p>\n<p>Luminar and Volvo didn&#8217;t reveal how much this highway pilot package might cost. Luminar has previously said its Iris lidar unit will cost less than $1,000 per unit for production vehicles seeking full autonomy and about $500 for version used for more limited purposes like driver assistance.<\/p>\n<p>The announcement is a milestone for Luminar and its whiz founder <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https:\/\/crunchbase.com\/person\/austin-russell\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"person\" data-entity=\"austin-russell\">Austin Russell, <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"><\/span><\/a> who burst onto the autonomous vehicle startup scene <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2017\/04\/13\/luminar-debuts-a-sensor-to-make-self-driving-cars-safer-than-human\/\">in April 2017<\/a> after operating for years in secrecy. It also makes Volvo the first automaker to equip production vehicles with lidar \u2014 the light detection and ranging radar that measures distance using laser light to generate a highly accurate 3D map of the world around the car.<\/p>\n<p>Luminar&#8217;s Iris lidar sensors \u2014 which <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https:\/\/crunchbase.com\/organization\/techcrunch\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"techcrunch\">TechCrunch <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"><\/span><\/a> has described as about the size of really thick sandwich and one-third smaller than its previous iterations \u2014 will be integrated in the roof. The sensor&#8217;s tucked away placement is a departure from the bucket style spinning lidars that have become synonymous with autonomous vehicle development.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_1984654\" style=\"width: 4106px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Volvo_SPA2_Luminar_Roofline_Integration-1.png\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-1984654\" class=\"breakout wp-image-1984654 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Volvo_SPA2_Luminar_Roofline_Integration-1.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"4096\" height=\"2160\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Volvo_SPA2_Luminar_Roofline_Integration-1.png 4096w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Volvo_SPA2_Luminar_Roofline_Integration-1.png?resize=150,79 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Volvo_SPA2_Luminar_Roofline_Integration-1.png?resize=300,158 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Volvo_SPA2_Luminar_Roofline_Integration-1.png?resize=768,405 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Volvo_SPA2_Luminar_Roofline_Integration-1.png?resize=680,359 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Volvo_SPA2_Luminar_Roofline_Integration-1.png?resize=1536,810 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Volvo_SPA2_Luminar_Roofline_Integration-1.png?resize=2048,1080 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/05\/Volvo_SPA2_Luminar_Roofline_Integration-1.png?resize=50,26 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 4096px) 100vw, 4096px\" \/><\/a><p id=\"caption-attachment-1984654\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Volvo<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>Shipping a vehicle with the proper hardware and perception stack doesn&#8217;t mean customers will be able to let their Volvo take over driving on highways from the get go. The software, which is being developed by <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https:\/\/crunchbase.com\/organization\/zenuity\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"zenuity\">Zenuity, <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"><\/span><\/a> is still underway, Volvo CTO Henrik Green said.<\/p>\n<p>The software will be activated wirelessly once it is verified to be safe in individual geographic locations. Volvo will continue to expand the capability of the software such as pushing up the maximum speed a vehicle can travel while driving autonomously. This hardware first-continual software update strategy is similar to <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https:\/\/crunchbase.com\/organization\/tesla-motors\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"tesla-motors\">Tesla, <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"><\/span><\/a> which has sold an automated driving package to consumers for years that has improved over time, but still does not allow for so-called &#8220;full self-driving.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Soon, your Volvo will be able to drive autonomously on highways when the car determines it is safe to do so,&#8221; Green said. &#8220;At that point, your Volvo takes responsibility for the driving and you can relax, take your eyes off the road and your hands off the wheel. Over time, updates over the air will expand the areas in which the car can drive itself. For us, a safe introduction of autonomy is a gradual introduction.&#8221;<\/p>\n<h2>A turning point for lidar<\/h2>\n<p>Lidar sensors are considered by many automakers and tech companies an essential piece of technology to safely roll out autonomous vehicles. In the past 18 months, as the timeline to deploy commercial robotaxi fleets has expanded, automakers have turned back to developing nearer term tech for production vehicles.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;It&#8217;s a very isolated problem to solve and becomes a lot more solvable in a safe way than trying to solve autonomous driving through the inner city of Los Angeles or San Francisco,&#8221; Green said. &#8220;By narrowing the use case to those particular highways, we can bring safe autonomy into vehicles for personal use in the timeframe we&#8217;re talking about.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>Advanced driver assistance systems, or ADAS, that was pushed aside in pursuit of fully autonomous vehicles has become a darling once again. It&#8217;s prompted a pivot within the industry, particularly with lidar companies. Dozens of lidar startups once grappling to become the supplier of choice for fully driverless vehicles are now hawking their wares for use in regular old passenger cars, trucks and SUVs. Some lidar startups such as Luminar have developed the perception software as well in an effort to diversify their business and offer a more appealing package to automakers.<\/p>\n<p>The companies will deepen their collaboration to ensure Luminar&#8217;s lidar technology is validated for series production. Volvo Cars said it has signed an agreement to possibly\u00a0increase its minority stake in Luminar.<\/p>\n<p>Luminar built its lidar from scratch, a lengthy process that it says has resulted in a simpler design and better performance. The company made a leap forward in April 2018 with the introduction of a<a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2018\/04\/12\/luminar-puts-its-lidar-tech-into-production-through-acquisitions-and-smart-engineering\/\"> new lidar unit<\/a> that performs better, is cheaper and is able to be assembled in minutes rather than hours. Luminar also acquired Black Forest Engineering as part of its strategy to improve the quality along with efficiency. And it opened a 136,000-square-foot manufacturing center in Orlando, Florida, where it does all of its engineering and development as well as the mass manufacturing.<\/p>\n<p>The startup has continued to improve its lidar as well as attract investors. Luminar announced last year it had <a href=\"https:\/\/www.businesswire.com\/news\/home\/20190711005233\/en\/Luminar-Drives-Expansion-Automotive-Market-250-Million\">raised $100 million<\/a>, bringing its total to more than $250 million. The company unveiled a perception platform and its compact Iris lidar unit, which will now go into the Volvo.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;This is really kind of the holy grail that we&#8217;ve been working towards for the entire course of the business,&#8221; Russell said.<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Volvo Cars will start producing vehicles in 2020 that are equipped with lidar and a perception stack \u2014 technology developed by Silicon Valley startup Luminar that the automaker will use to deploy an automated driving system for highways. For now, the lidar will be part of a hardware package that consumers can add as an
